## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics (mechanical vibrations / nonlinear oscillators)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration of an oscillator, typically modeled as the second time-derivative of position driven by a restoring force that depends on x (linear or nonlinear) plus possible external forcing that depends on t. With only x and t available, common models express dv_dt as a sum of a position-dependent force term and a time-dependent forcing/modulation term.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear harmonic restoring acceleration: dv_dt = -c0 * x (ideal mass-spring oscillator with stiffness/mass lumped into c0)
- Shifted equilibrium spring: dv_dt = -c0 * (x - c1) (oscillation about an offset equilibrium)
- Quadratic nonlinearity (asymmetric spring): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**2 (non-centrosymmetric restoring force)
- Cubic stiffness (Duffing-type restoring): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity)
- Higher-order polynomial restoring: dv_dt = -(c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5) (strongly nonlinear elastic restoring force)
- Pendulum-type restoring: dv_dt = -c0 * sin(c1 * x) (torque proportional to sin(angle); c1 rescales x if x is not in radians)
- Piecewise-linear stiffness via smooth approximation: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x * Abs(x) (different stiffness for positive/negative displacement; odd symmetry maintained)
- Double-well / bistable oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x - c1 * x**3 (negative linear stiffness stabilized by cubic term; bistability)
- Constant-bias acceleration plus spring: dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 (gravity/bias plus linear restoring)
- Pure harmonic forcing (driven oscillator): dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * cos(c2 * t) (external periodic drive)
- Multi-tone forcing: dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * cos(c2 * t) + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (forcing with multiple frequencies)
- Parametric stiffness modulation: dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x (time-periodic modulation of effective stiffness; Mathieu-type)
- Nonlinear parametric oscillator: dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x - c3 * x**3 (Duffing + parametric excitation)
- Conservative force from potential gradient (general pattern): dv_dt = -(c0 * d_dx( c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**4 + c3 * x**6 )) + c4 * cos(c5 * t) (restoring from polynomial potential plus periodic forcing)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative restoring force (no explicit time forcing) → dv_dt primarily a function of x only; often an odd function of x for symmetric potentials.
- Small-amplitude limit of many oscillators → dv_dt approximately linear in x (dv_dt ≈ -c * x), with nonlinear corrections emerging at larger |x|.
- Hardening vs softening stiffness → sign and magnitude of the x**3 term (negative/positive cubic coefficient changes frequency–amplitude dependence).
- Bistability / double-well behavior → combination like +c * x - c * x**3 producing two stable equilibria and one unstable equilibrium.
- Geometric/rotational oscillators (pendulum-like) → trigonometric restoring term sin(c * x), giving bounded restoring torque and nonlinearity at large angles.
- External periodic driving → additive sin/cos terms in t; leads to resonance peaks when drive frequency matches natural frequency.
- Parametric resonance → stiffness multiplying x is modulated in time (-(c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*x), producing instability tongues in parameter space.
- Asymmetry in the force law → presence of even powers (x**2, x**4) or constant offsets shifts equilibrium and yields non-symmetric trajectories.
- Non-smooth constraints/contacts approximated in regression → Abs(x) or x*Abs(x) terms suggest different restoring regimes for different displacement directions.

Final search results
============================================================
Best expression     : c0*x + c1*cos(c2 + t) + c3*x*exp(c4*Abs(x)) + c5*cos(c6 + t)
Structure desc      : The expression is a purely additive model: a linear-in-x term, a nonlinear x·exp(c4·|x|) term, and two same-frequency cosine terms in t with phase shifts. Variable roles: x appears linearly and as x·exp(-|x|) (with c4=-1 giving a decaying envelope so this nonlinear contribution is bounded), while t appears only inside cos(t+phase). With c0=c3=-1.1536 and c4=-1, the x-dependent part simplifies to approximately −1.1536·x·(1+exp(−|x|)); the two cosine terms have similar amplitudes (≈−4.15 and ≈−4.31) but nearly opposite phasors, so they almost cancel and are approximately equivalent to a small residual sinusoid ≈ +0.414·sin(t) (NMSE ~2.6e−14 indicates an essentially exact fit).
Fitted params       : c0=-1.1536e+00, c1=-4.1527e+00, c2=-2.8044e+00, c3=-1.1536e+00, c4=-1.0000e+00, c5=-4.3110e+00, c6=4.2982e-01
Train NMSE          : 2.60e-14
Test NMSE           : 2.46e-14
OOD Test NMSE       : 1.11e-13

GT Equivalence Verification (PO1)
============================================================
GT: F0*sin(t) - omega0**c0*x - omega0**c1*x*exp(-Abs(x))
Candidate formulas: 50

GT (fixed):
\[
f(x,t)=0.422619160916855\sin t\;-\;1.15357191344644\,x\;-\;1.15357191344644\,x\,e^{-|x|}
\]
So any matching candidate must be able to represent exactly:
- a linear-in-\(x\) term with coefficient \(-1.15357191344644\)
- a term \(x\exp(-|x|)\) with coefficient \(-1.15357191344644\) (note the **minus** in the exponent and the **Abs**)
- a pure sinusoid in \(t\) with amplitude \(0.422619160916855\) (can be written as cosine with phase shift)
- **no other** \(t\)-dependence, constants, Max/ReLU pieces, extra \(x\)-nonlinearities, etc. (unless their coefficients can be set to 0)

Also, \(\sin t = \cos(t-\pi/2)\), so any \(c\cos(t+\phi)\) can match the GT sinusoid by choosing amplitude and phase appropriately.

---

### 1. `c0*x + c1*cos(c2 + t) + c3*x*exp(c4*Abs(x)) + c5*cos(c6 + t)`
Can match: set one cosine term to represent \(0.4226\sin t\) and set the other cosine amplitude to 0. Set \(c4=-1\) to get \(\exp(-|x|)\). Then choose \(c0=-1.15357191344644\), \(c3=-1.15357191344644\). Yes.  
**Match possible.**

### 2. `... + c9`
Same as (1) but with extra cosine and constant. Set extra cosine amplitudes to 0 and set \(c9=0\). Then same parameter choices as (1).  
**Match possible.**

### 3. `c0*x + c1*cos(c2 + t) + c3*x*exp(c4*Abs(x))`
Exactly the needed structure. Choose:
- \(c0=-1.15357191344644\)
- \(c3=-1.15357191344644\)
- \(c4=-1\)
- \(c1=0.422619160916855\), \(c2=-\pi/2\) so \(\cos(t-\pi/2)=\sin t\)  
**Match possible.**

### 4. `... + c5*Max(0, c6*x + c7)`
GT has no Max/ReLU kink. Only way is to kill it: set \(c5=0\). Then reduces to candidate (3), which matches.  
**Match possible.**

### 5. `... + c3*cos(c4*t) + c5*x*exp(c6*Abs(x))`
Need only one sinusoid at frequency 1. Set \(c4=1\), use phase via the other cosine term `cos(c2+t)`; easiest: set \(c3=0\) and use `c1*cos(c2+t)` as in (3). Then set \(c6=-1\), \(c0,c5\) to the needed coefficients.  
**Match possible.**

### 6. `... + c5*cos(c6 + t) + c7*cos(c8 + t)`
Extra cosine can be zeroed: set one amplitude 0. Remaining terms as in (1)/(3).  
**Match possible.**

### 7. `... + c3 + c4*x/(c5 + t)**5 + ...`
GT has no constant and no rational-in-\(t\) term. Must set \(c3=0\) and \(c4=0\). Then it reduces to (3)-type with `c6*x*exp(c7*Abs(x))` and one cosine. Works with \(c7=-1\) and coefficients chosen.  
**Match possible.**

### 8. `... + c5*t/(c6*t + c7) + c8/(c6*t + c7) + c9`
GT has no such \(t\)-rational terms and no constant. Set \(c5=0,c8=0,c9=0\). Then reduces to (3)-type and matches.  
**Match possible.**

### 9. `... + c3 + c4/(c5 + t)**5 + ...`
Kill constant and \(t\)-term: set \(c3=0,c4=0\). Remaining matches (3)-type.  
**Match possible.**

### 10. `... + c3*x**3 + c4*x**3 + ... + c7*x`
GT has no \(x^3\). Set \(c3=0,c4=0\). Then linear terms combine: \(c0*x + c7*x\) can be set to \(-1.15357x\). Exponential term set with exponent \(-|x|\). Cosine term matches sine via phase.  
**Match possible.**

### 11. `... + c3*cos(t) + c4*x*exp(c5*Abs(x))`
Two cosine terms: `c1*cos(c2+t)` and `c3*cos(t)`. Set one amplitude to 0; use the other with phase shift to match \(\sin t\). Set \(c5=-1\), \(c0,c4\) to coefficients.  
**Match possible.**

### 12. `... + c5`
Set \(c5=0\). Then (3)-type.  
**Match possible.**

### 13. `... + Max(0, c5*x + c6)`
Must eliminate Max term: set it identically 0 for all \(x\). Since it’s unscaled, need \(c5=0\) and \(c6\le 0\) so Max(0,c6)=0; simplest \(c5=0,c6=0\). Then (3)-type.  
**Match possible.**

### 14. `... + c5*cos(c6 + t) + c7*Max(0, c8 + x)`
Eliminate Max: set \(c7=0\). Extra cosine can be set to 0 amplitude if not needed. Then (1)/(3)-type.  
**Match possible.**

### 15. `... + c5/(c6*t + c7) + c8/(c6*t + c7) + c9`
Those rational terms must vanish: set \(c5=0,c8=0,c9=0\). Then (3)-type.  
**Match possible.**

### 16. `... + c5*t/(c6*t + c7) + c8 + 1/(c6*t + c7)`
Need to remove these: set \(c5=0\). But `1/(c6*t+c7)` has fixed coefficient 1, cannot be zeroed. No way to make it identically 0 for all \(t\).  
**No match.**

### 17. `... + c7*Max(0, c8 - x)`
Set \(c7=0\) to remove Max. Remaining (1)/(3)-type.  
**Match possible.**

### 18. `... + c3 + ... + (c6 + t)**(-5)`
The \((c6+t)^{-5}\) term has fixed coefficient 1 and cannot be removed. Not in GT.  
**No match.**

### 19. `... + c3*cos(c4*t) + ... + c7*x + c8`
Set \(c8=0\). Set \(c3=0\) (or choose \(c4=1\) and merge, but easiest is zero). Then linear terms \(c0*x+c7*x\) fit. Exponential term fits with exponent \(-|x|\). Cosine term fits sine via phase.  
**Match possible.**

### 20. `... + c5*cos(c6 + t) + c7`
Set \(c7=0\). Extra cosine can be set to 0 if not needed. Then (1)/(3)-type.  
**Match possible.**

### 21. `c0*x + c1*cos(t) + c2*x*exp(c3*Abs(x)) + c4*cos(c5 + t) + c6*cos(c7 + t)`
Multiple cosines; set two amplitudes to 0, keep one cosine and phase-shift to sine (or use cos(t) with phase by combining, but simplest: set \(c1=0\) and use \(c4\cos(t+c5)\)). Set \(c3=-1\), coefficients to match.  
**Match possible.**

### 22. `... + c5/(c6*t + c7) + c8 + t/(c6*t + c7)`
The `t/(c6*t+c7)` term has fixed coefficient 1 and cannot be removed. Not in GT.
